RATING: 10
This game is fantastic.  A quick, fun, cutthroat game that has wonderful mechanics and an excellent theme.  Remembering where your high point value members are adds an element of memory that makes it a bluffing game a well, though it is equally fun to ignore that aspect of placement and just scramble to get as many as possible to safety.  

Truly a game that should appeal to everybody--definitely give this one a try if you have not played it before, no matter what your favorite type of game is.

RATING: 8.5
Mass hysteria. An incredibly simple and organic experience, pitting players against a crumbling island surrounded by sharks, whales, and sea monsters. These survivors can be ruthless, though, as they are given the opportunity for control over these predators.

The beauty of this game is the lack of complexity. It's an outwit and out-move situation, but it is also a game of social negotiation and memory. Every little survivor is worth a secret amount of points. Players can only view the amounts of their own survivors at the beginning of the game, as they are setting them out on the board. After that, you better remember who your valuable survivors are and get them to safety! You may have to team up with an opponent, offering help to their survivors in exchange for safe passage of your own or perhaps a little mercy from the movement of sharks. 

Survive plays quick, with an emphasis on laughter, tension, and shouting. Lots and lots of shouting! Be careful who you play this with, because if they can't handle a bit of the cutthroat, it may not go over so well. For all others, this is one of those games that brings friendly competition and laughs every minute.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Survive is a tactical game with so much chaos around you that there is really no point trying to devise any grand strategies. Of course, it is better to have some kind of a plan but essentially you just play the move that fits the situation at hand.

There is a clear dramatic arc in the game, which is nice. The island is sinking, people get killed while some survive but the game inevitably comes to an end. 

I also feel compelled to compare Survive with the game it reimplements (Escape from Atlantis). Personally I find the latter more exciting with beautiful 3D components. The rule changes are for the worse, as well. First of all, having meeples of different (secret) VP value makes it much harder to see who is winning. Basically this just introduces more uncontrollable elements to a game that is very chaotic already. This is maybe the biggest bad change. Moreover, the more restricted movement of sea creatures is a change that is very euro in nature. I prefer the rule of the original that with some (bad) luck creatures can occasionally jump to any free space. This creates more excitement since you are not guaranteed to reach safety at any point. Ok, first I am complaining about introducing more chaos and then I want to have more. However, the two things work in a very different way. The first one is totally out of control while the latter depends on players' choices.

Anyways, not a bad game but having played the original, I'll stick to it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Ameritrash at its best. You are a tribe of meeples on Atlantis that is in the process of sinking into the ocean. You want to get on boats and or swim, (swimming is a last resort believe me) off the doomed island and to shore of another continent. Certain of your meeples are worth more points than others but you won't know if you don't remember after placement, and they will be competing with other meeple tribes for the scarce boats. On your turn you take another piece of the island away, which usually involves making someone's meeple/s take a bath, and trigger or hold onto a special power. Then you move your meeples and boats and roll a die. This leads to you moving whales that destroy boats, Sharks that eat meeples in the ocean, and monsters that destroy boats and eat meeples. So, the game isn't a coop is what I am saying. As long as everyone is a good sport, than this game plays like a wonderful scramble for safety where a lot of take that and mayhem occurs. Beware playing with happy cooperative people, it breaks the game.

RATING: 8.1
I had my eye on this for a while, and it has lived up to all of my expectations!  I am not at all surprised this is a classic.

The one negative I can think of is that there is a fair amount of luck involved.  Some players will flip over more beneficial tiles, experience better creature die rolls, etc.  The luck involved does affect my rating, but only slightly.

On the other hand, there are many positives to mention.  The variable setup is definitely a plus.  More than likely, you will start with a unique island every time.  I also like the variable ending, insofar as you don't know exactly when the volcano tile--which triggers the end of the game immediately--will be drawn.

One of the major points on the plus side for this game are the short turns.  This broadens the potential player pool for this game considerably, and makes it a great selection as a "gateway game."  It also renders it a family game, so long as you are OK with the somewhat violent theme (people are constantly dying, after all).  You will "get the game" halfway through your first game, and start playing very fast turns.  The game plays in 45 minutes, as advertised.

Finally, I find the theme appealing.  Yes, people are dying left and right, but trying to get your people to safety whilst avoiding numerous hazards is quite thrilling.  And the mechanics do fit the theme, to be sure!  For example, if you're flailing about in the sea, you have to spend an action (you get 3 per turn) to climb into a boat, onto adjacent land, etc.

In conclusion, I really like this game and can recommend it to almost everyone; I have a feeling this will get a lot of table time in my house.

RATING: 9
A very fun family game with tremendous appeal.  Features a very simple yet thoughtful ruleset; allowing players to quickly and easily understand how to both play and strategize.  The components are all beautiful, with cool meeples and well designed tiles (particularly in the easy to understand symbols).  Only gripe I have however is that my copy came with some marked meeples, but I have contacted Stronghold Games and do expect that they will make good soon enough.  Survive! plays very fast with times fluctuating between 30 to 60 minutes (with most games finishing well under an hour).

All in all what do you have with this?

(1) A great theme (to bring in the family, non-gamers and kiddies), 
(2) simple, deep rules (easily allowing clever play), 
(3) fantastic components, 
(4) and all of this combines into a tremendous game played best with the full accompaniment of four.  Get it!

Update: Stronghold Games did indeed make good on my component request, swiftly sending me in the meeples I requested.  Thank you!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Nasty little game of extreme screwage.  When competitive adults are involved keep kids out of this game or they will be permanently scarred.  Make that island tile disappear, drop the other players piece into the ocean and let the sharks get him, haha!  We laugh all the way through this, especially if someone complains that we're picking on him.

Downfall of Pompeii has a similar theme, but plays very different.  Survive! is very much an AmeriTrash game, while Downfall of Pompeii plays like a Euro, and is much less random.

The stronghold version has great production quality.  No more thin cardboard pieces.  The lifeboats in particular are great.  However if you get the Stronghold version, I'd really recommend purchasing the 5-6 player expansion for the replacement meeples and hexes, which take care of some issues in the original.

Plays best with 4

RATING: 5
For a game that was first published in 1982, it's quite amazing that it manages to compete against more modern titles. Undoubtedly, this stems from a very clean design, which has mechanics that mesh well with the theme and that allow for some interesting strategic choices. 

But despite appreciating the design, this game can be quite confrontational. Granted, some of the "meanness" can be mitigated by understanding the importance of coupling your meeples with your opponent meeples, in order to "piggy-back." But it still requires a certain mindset/playing-style to enjoy. 

The component quality of the 30th anniversary is absolutely amazing. Stronghold Games really knocked it out of the park with this release.

RATING: 4
Atlantis' flagship mechanic is, without doubt, Take That. This game is all about smashing your opponents while attempting to slip a couple of your guys past their radar. It's simple, easy to understand, and actually quite fun. More fun than being eaten by sharks at least. I'd appreciate a bit more control, but this game really isn't about meticulously strategizing your moves. An additional downside is that the game has a tendency of fizzling out towards the end, with all the important moves having been done in the first few rounds.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I can see why this game would have been a classic back in the 80s, because it broke from the traditional roll-and-move mold that was so prevalent. The way the game works is great because it almost demands some cooperation, and yet you're cooperating with the same people who will eat your people with a sea serpent or shark 2 turns later. The hidden points also lend a good amount of drama because you never know who exactly is winning until the final scores are tallied. I always feel the need to preface this game as one where "you have to be comfortable with being mean and nasty to each other" and that can turn off some players. Yet somehow the group that has embraced this game the most is my family, and they have requested it often. The biggest downside to the game is the length, because it can sometimes drag out a bit longer than necessary, especially when played with slow thinkers. I also think a lot of the variant rules are unnecessary and don’t add much to the experience. This is kind of a bummer because people see the dolphins and want to play with them, but they add some unnecessary confusion to the game. However these complaints are minor compared to the fun we have playing the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.5
New gamer friendly... easy mechanics, easy to explain, and potentially hilarious.

The gameplay is mediocre with some odd design aspects. For example, whales and sharks don't populate until their tiles are revealed; thus as the island disappears, more creatures fill the board. So there is a huge advantage (and sometimes this determines the winner) for those who rush to safety in the beginning. 

A story...
My friend loaded up his boat with 3 people. Before his next turn, a whale had been revealed and moved to destroy the boat. Using another boat in a rescue operation, he managed to move the whale and get the boat into the same hex as the original 3 people. By his third turn, another whale was revealed and destroyed his second boat. Having 4 people in one hex off of the beach, we all laughed at what looked like a spring break party. Then someone revealed a whirlpool and wiped out everything. Obviously, he spent the rest of the game vowing retribution. 

This game is a strategically-vacant killing spree of unpreventable scenarios. It is truly a game of survival, I just wish that surviving was less random.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Waddington's classic family board game sadly long out of print (North American version made around the same time by Parker Bros was remodeled and called "Survive"). A remote island with an active, threatening volcano is also slowly sinking into the ocean. Ten "people" in four different player colours are stranded on the island trying to escape by either swimming or commandeering several small boats scattered about the coast.

Players take turns moving their people/boats then removing a tile (reflecting the erosion of the island), starting with sand, then jungle, and finally the rocky areas (beneath one of which is the symbol of the volcano erupting which ends the game). Finally the player rolls a special die which has faces representing either a shark, whale or sea-serpent and can move the figure rolled, if there is one available, to plague the opponents. Each tile removed has a back-printed symbol adding more sea creatures to the board, or more boats, or may become an "event card" to be played later by the player to aid in moving his people or killing marauding sea creature.

The game is relatively simple and while listed as being for ages "eight and up" can be played and enjoyed by younger children as long as an older person is available to provide some coaching. It is very enjoyable for all ages and provides some delicious tension as the island gets smaller and smaller, more sea creatures roam about the struggling survivors and the threat of the volcano looms ever closer. Why no-one has seen fit to reprint this gem remains a mystery!
++++++
Mystery no more! It's back and with a brand new suit of clothes. Not as three dimensional as the original Waddington version but very nice compared to the Parker Bros entry. No need to re-write any of the rules - this enduring classic is fun for all ages - we've been using it lately as a session ending filler.

RATING: 4
Rating is based on the "Waddington" version (3D island pieces, die with 3 dolphins on it, and people-shaped bits), as played a few times.  Current impressions:  cool-looking bits, fun game, but somewhat random.  Annoyances:  the people bits are quite unstable (a big deal in a fiddly game like this), the rules are vague on some issues, whirlpool action seems to make the game really random, the monster die comes up "dolphin" a lot more than necessary, and the hexes are too small for the size of of the bits that are supposed to fit in them (particularly in combination).  This is one of the games I am keeping because other people in my life enjoy playing them.  I'd be just fine if I never played this one again.  Bash the leader problem, big advantage to the start player, too long for what it is, very chaotic.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
First play: This went over very well with the 3 others I played with.  Easy to teach, with simple mechanics, but it quickly became clear that there's more to this game than first appears.  The game encourages confrontation, since you have to do something with those sea monsters and sharks you keep rolling, but it's also light enough that it's hard to feel too bad when your guy is gobbled by a shark.  

First impression is that this hits the sweet spot of being quite accessible to non-gamers (who make up the bulk of my opponents), but having enough depth to be fun for me too.  I like it.

Second play: 2er.  Significantly less interesting than the 4er game.  I didn't think more control could hurt a game, but it does here.  Half the excitement is wondering what's going to happen between turns.  It's also decidedly more vicious with 2, and not in a good way.

RATING: 6
This is a fun game. While the strategy is pretty minimal and you can't fairly compare it fairness/balance wise to most modern euros, everything about this game is just fun and intuitive. The walking, swimming, whale/shark rules all sort of make sense, which helps make the game flow pretty well.

Also, it's just a ton of fun to turn over a whirlpool tile that kills everyone else's helpless people, who have just been tossed out of their boats by a whale. There's also nothing quite like watching another player's people slowly getting surrounded by whales and sea serpents, and the sense of dread that there's just no way that they're going to make it...

It is certainly very luck heavy -- in my first play I received zero tiles that help movement, and ended up with a score of 0, and the winner received a ton of those tiles. So as long as you go in for the entertaining carnage / survivor experience and not a strategy game you won't be disappointed.  The new edition board is also gorgeous.

Initial rating an 8. I'd potentially rate it even higher, except for the overwhelming luck involved and the fact that it is slightly on the long side for this type of game.

RATING: 10
It's hard to put into words why this is so fun - it's just a simple, heated, well-designed game. It feels like it has a pretty good balance between strategy (moving through action points, spending your hand tiles) and luck (land tiles, dice.) The pacing is swift and spot-on.

I can't imagine this being as good with less than four... having EVERY land space filled from the beginning is awesome.

This game can be pretty mean, but in a hilarious way (who doesn't think tossing a sea monsters at your friends is funny?) and since everyone is CONSTANTLY doing something "bad" it's not that big a deal when you have some dudes eaten.

Oh, it's also a perfect length. Long enough to be satisfying while short enough that the "one more play" impulse is pretty strong. Good stuff!

Update: Fuck it, Survive, you've earned your 10. Every time I bust you out I have a blast, and when it's over I think to myself that there are few ways to spend your hour that are equally laugh-filled and fun.

Update the Second: It seems silly, but I upgraded from the third Stronghold edition to the 30th anniversary one via a trade. My meeples had worn to illegibility, and it really is one of my favorite games. Gonna gift the third away to a family member so I can always play it when visiting!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Update: Now I have played it as an adult and many other designs have caught up and surpassed it.  It was way ahead of its time in 1983 but 29 years have dulled the thrill.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Survive was one of my favorite games from my childhood. I even still remember the TV commercial and theme song for it. I was lucky enough to receive the updated version as a gift.

This game was genius back in the day, and it has stood the test of time fairly well. It's certainly random, but not much more than other gateway options. What makes this game so darn fun is the theme and the "take that" nature of play. With two, I'm thinking it's probably best to play two colors with each player. There's not enough risk and press your luck with only two player colors. 

The new edition is very attractive. My only two gripes are 1) the numbers are hard to read on the blue meeples and 2) the backs of certain rock tiles punched out with a white border, which stinks when one supposedly random tile ends the game. On the other hand, I admire that the reprint includes tweaks past the original version, with dolphins, new dice, etc. Throw in the squid expansion, and there's a lot of ways to customize this fun little game to your liking. 

Update: 2nd play, this time with the dolphins on the board. It wasn't as bloody as I expected, as the die tended to produce boat and dolphin movement, which balanced out a three hex movement from a swimmer-chomping-sea-serpent. This is probably the better way to play.

[b]key update[/b]: A major "kudos" for Stronghold Games. Unprompted, Stronghold reached out to me regarding the misprinted rock tiles. They must have been perusing user comments (!!!) and actively sought out the few people that received games with this misprint, offering a free replacement. I'm flabbergasted! This type of superior customer service is fantastic. Bravo Stronghold!

...and final update: traded this away along with the 5-6 player expansion for the Claustrophobia: De Profundis expansion. I had a lot of nostalgia for this game, but with a handful of plays under my belt, it started to show its age a bit. It's a good game, and surprisingly good for its time, but I didn't need to own this one. The nostalgia hid some of the game's minor flaws. For me, the biggest flaw is that the endgame is not terribly exciting, as people have mostly reached the outer islands (or their guys are dead), and it's just waiting to draw that last tile. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A classic secret deployment game that truly stands the test of time. You have to get your meeples off the sinking island in the center of the board to one of the small docks at each of the corners. Of course you have all sorts of sea creatures chasing you and your opponents trying to get their meeples to the docks ahead of yours. It's deliciously cutthroat and leads to a lot of laughs around the table. It serves as a great family game as long as people don't mind a few hurt feelings. The only downside is remembering all your meeple values and trying to not knock them over as they really need a wider base in order to truly keep them secret as we kept having problems with them falling over.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Cute mainstream game that is accessible enough to play with the kids while still offering some decision space for the adults. Players each control a stable of people with hidden victory point values on their bottoms. The pawns are seeded out onto an island that is sinking and surrounding by various man-eating beasts such as sea serpents and sharks. A few boats are also present. The goal is to get the people (either by boat or backstroke) to 4 safe islands on the corners of the board.

Each turn players move their own pieces, then remove a chunk from the central island, and then unleash a monster of the deep, which is randomly chosen via a die.

The game ends when one of the later tiles is flipped over which reveals a volcano on its backside, the surviving pawns are checked, and most VPs wins.

Survive is not a hardcore strategy game by any means, but it offers some good decision space, is fast-paced, and is enjoyable to play on occasion, provided that you don't have someone who is too sensitive about getting whacked on the head, because there's a lot of that present here. (i.e.: I could see this being a nightmare with some kids...and some adults I know for that matter). Though the scoring scheme and cleverness of the shrinking board presages the coming Euro invasion in some ways, the gratuitous and completely over the top player hosing reminds you that this is still very much an American design.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game doesn't just play like a Eurogame, it is also better than most Eurogames.  It is extremely simple yet it has a lot of room for planning and decision making and there is a great, layered sense of drama- getting off the sinking island paired with getting your men to islands on the other side of shark, whale, and sea monster-infested waters.  There are a couple of minor issues, the boats seem too rare and easy to get rid of and the endgame is somewhat anticlimatic but nonetheless this is a neglected classic.

RATING: 8
A lost gem that thankfully was reprinted recently.  Not for players who don't like direct confrontation, since this game is truly a bloodbath (sharks, whales, and sea monsters!). Much better for three or four players, but still enjoyable for two, there is a constant feeling of adventure and suspense.  The theme of the game matches perfectly with the game play mechanics.  Pure fun for all ages, unless you happen to be a soft-hearted innocent and just want everyone to survive!  Sinking an opponent's piece by removing a tile that just happens to be a shark waiting to eat them is probably one of the most satisfying experiences in gaming.
A vicious game that finds a happy medium between luck and strategy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This game reminds me a bit of Small World - you have to be mean to other players, but since it's happening constantly all around, it's hard to take it personally.

On a rapidly disappearing island of tiles, players try to rescue their pawns by boat or (much more slowly) swimming.  Dangers abound from whales, sharks and sea serpents.  Some tiles will reveal special abilities to help players along.  At the end you flip over your pawns to reveal their values - can you remember which ones were worth the most?

This game has a high degree of randomness, which could turn off some players.  But it's a fun way to start off or end an evening on a light note.  Try to survive!

RATING: 4
Fine for what it is, but lighter than I like, and it's just got just enough things going on that it can take longer than I want to be playing it. I'd enjoy it a lot more with either or both of:

* Something to smooth the variance in tile draws - drawing a dolphin is phenomenal, drawing a "relocate a whale" is OK, drawing "add a whale" is meh. Perhaps in a 2p game the luck of the draw evens out over time, but not in 4p.

* A 15-to-20-second turn timer, to promote the feeling of panic and fleeing - embracing its nature as an experience game rather than something super-strategic. (If you don't finish your turn in time, you forfeit some/all of your move actions the following turn.)

I quite like the dynamics of shared boats vs. single-player boats.

RATING: 6
Components: Great components in the Stronghold edition. The text is difficult to read on the dark blue meeples, but that has been corrected with the sticker insets in the expansion.
The different height tiles and shaped wooden bits really help the theme.

Experience: This game is all over the map. I was playing vicious, targeting whomever I thought was in the lead, and trying to give my opponents opportunities to do the same. Other opponents were playing nicer, letting boats full of people just skirt by the nasties. The game seems to support both styles of play.

The random setup at the beginning, and the random undersides of tiles should help to keep the game interesting for several plays.

Eagerness to Play Again: Within a year

RATING: 9
Upon first play with my 7 year old daughter, I really enjoyed this game. The rules were quite easy to learn and teach; everything is intuitive. The components are wonderful; nice thick wood pieces, solid card stock, and nice plastic meeples.  The game play was really entertaining - putting meeples on boats, knocking them overboard with whales, eating them up with sharks.  This game was a blast and I totally want to play it again!  With the added expansion making this playable with 6... I can see getting a lot of replay value. EXCELLENT!

P.S. The only negative I found in the two player was that whales were not as useful in the game.  If I shared a boat with my opponent, I generally don't want to attack it with a whale.  I found we just merely moved whales around the board.  (This game is most likely better with 3 or more players).  I will have to wait to see if my rating changes with more plays.  None-the-less, I am hyped about this game after my first play!

Edit after 3 plays: played with 5 players and the game runs a little slow (due to AP) but it is still fun. More cut-throat action for sure!

Edit after 5 plays: This is an AWESOME family game!!!!  I have played it with my 4 and 7 year old daughters - they both got the hang of the game and we had loads of fun.  I highly recommend this game to families regardless of the competitive nature; just preload the kids before play

RATING: N/A
$30 Amazon
Survive is a cutthroat game where players seek to evacuate their pieces from an island that is breaking up, while remembering where their highest-valued pieces are located to maximize their score. An island made up of 40 hex-tiles is slowly sinking into the ocean (as the tiles are removed from the board). Each player controls ten people (valued from 1 to 6) that they try and move towards the safety of the surrounding islands before the main island finally blows up. Players can either swim or use boats to travel but must avoid sea serpents, whales and sharks on their way to safety.

RATING: 7.75
[21 Jul 2016] - 7.75 (3 plays @ 6 players, 1 play @ 3 players)
This game thrives on nasty player interactions. The goal is to get your meeples off the sinking island while avoiding being eaten by sharks, sea monsters or having the boat destroyed by whales. Without the direct conflict, the game is just a boring exercise in trying to beat the game timer. You have to be willing to gang up on the leader and go after everyone. There is a bit of randomness when you draw the island tile and rolling the hazzard die.

At 6 players the game feels like a race to get safe before something bad happens. You end up tagging along with other players and going full board with the highest value meeples first in an attempt to score points. Being 3 or 4 in the turn order is a huge disadvantage since you lose out on the moving early but don't get an extra boat placement. Once you start falling behind, it's very tough to get back into the game.

At 3 players the game is a little more controlled. You'll get meeples off the island so it's going to be a game or remembering where the high value ones are and not alerting other players to them. Early rounds will have less direct conflict and it's easier to setup longer moves.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9.2
This is one of those games that never disappoints. Ever. It's hardly spectacular, but never dull. Better with 3 players, best with 4, this is a cutthroat game where you attempt to guide your prospective survivors off a sinking island to 1 of 4 safe shores, all the while avoiding sea creatures and other dangers that are controlled by the other players on their turns. There are no weak components here: the land tiles really pop due to the varying thicknesses, the wooden pieces are nice, and the small survivors have some weight to them. There is a reason this game has staying power.

RATING: 10
When I first heard about this re-release I was not that interested.  Unfortunately, part of this lack of interest had to do with prejudice: why should I care about a game from the 80s?  When I first got into board games more seriously I had a tendency to eschew the older games not realizing that there are a lot of gems.  I am amazed at how good this game is.  Survive is one of the most cutthroat games I have ever played, but it is also the kind of game you can play without really caring about who wins.  The most enjoyable games are the ones in which there are hardly any survivors.  There is certainly a lot of luck, but not so much that there are no meaningful decisions to make.

RATING: 7.5
A nostalgic game from my childhood, but it seems to have held up really well and is still quite fun.  In fact, the family-strategy style of this game, and the cool tile flipping mechanic, are what eventually led me to look into newer board games and discover the world of eurogames!

Update: I just replayed this one again, and even with only 2 players, it was much better than I remembered.  I'm looking forward to trying it with more players.  Not only did it lead me to the world of Euro games, I think it also acted as an inspiration for some Euro mechanics.  A classic!

RATING: 7

The wooden meeples are a bit of a misfire, as they are not consistent in size or thickness which can make the secret values not secret at all.   There's a lot of randomness in this game, especially with the tile flipping, but it's not a game to take too seriously anyways.

It is a game that teaches you to be a cutthroat double crossing b*****d. The island is slowly sinking and your goal is to have your worthiest survivors on the safe edges of the board. To achieve that you are going to step over the drowning, helpless meeples of your so called friends, you are going to sink the island under their feet and you are going to send all sorts of sea creatures to eat them or crush their hopes. And you are going to laugh about it!

The length of the game is few minutes too long to be a filler but it's perfect small party game. Expansions are bloating the game to below enjoyment and I would not recommend any of them. The base game is just fine.

RATING: 9
I grew up playing this game in the 80's, and was always bummed that I could never get my hands on a copy (darn collectors driving up the cost of my childhood memories!!!). HOWEVER, never fear, because the gaming industry finally did something that benefits me; they re-released this game, preserving the feel and function, AND drastically improving the board and playing pieces. I am shocked, and very pleased with this edition. I think it is quite possibly better than the original, and now I am glad I didn't spend 100 dollars on a collectors edition on ebay!!!

BUT, Let's talk shop:

The game board is way bigger than the original, and all the game components are vastly superior in quality. The rules are pretty much exactly as I remember, but I don't remember it being so difficult to keep all your boats. With 4 competitive players playing blood and guts rules (is there another kind?), I would be surprised if there were any boats left at the end.

What I like the most about the game is the island tiles. The thickness varies with the terrain, with the mountain and jungle tiles increasing in thickness, very cool.

The internal storage is awesome, with EXACT spots for all the components. This is a big plus with me because, lets face it, your games unfortunately spend A LOT more time in storage than they do in play mode. So why are the insides of most games seemingly designed by blind monkeys, with absolutely no thought to component storage?

I'm looking at YOU designers of Agricola!!!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a great light weight and chaotic free-for-all.  The rules are pretty simple to learn and the play time is right around an hour or less depending on player number and familiarity with the game.  

The goal is to move your pawns from a sinking Atlantis island to the surrounding safe zones, while dodging sea serpents, sharks, and whales.  If you're picking this one up, I would recommend getting the mini-expansions as well, but they aren't necessary.  The expansions add dolphins and giant squid, and increase the chaos and carnage of the original game.

My group has greatly enjoyed this game for what it is.  You won't find deep strategy here, but it fits the gap between short fillers and the longer, meatier games.   

Players who don't like too much chaos and hate having their game plans messed with should probably stay away from this one.  The game has a high amount of randomness and direct player conflict.  Recommended!  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I love this game. Every player gets 10 tokens so spread around a sinking island. The sand begins to sink first, then the forest, then the mountains. When an eruption occurs, game over! Anyone left on land tiles that aren't safe, or that are left in the sea will die. As the game progresses, everyone manipulates sharks, whales, and boats. Your meeple tokens have points on the bottoms of them that you're allowed to see only one time, and that's during the phase where you alternate populating the island. Any meeples that have made it to safe shores are flipped over at the end of the game to count up the points. This is a great family and friend game that's not hard to learn or teach at all. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4.5
After one play.

Simple game of take that, with a bit of memory and tactical maneuvering. I went into the game with fairly low expectations, wanting only a fun, short game to play with non-gamers. The non-gamers said they enjoyed it, but they didn't demonstrate the same kind of enthusiasm they'd shown for other gateway games, like Machi Koro. I was disappointed--it just wasn't very fun, though I'm not sure why. The take that mechanic feels so simplified that it lacks tension, whereas in more complex executions you could derive greater satisfaction in screwing up someone else's plans. Here it just feels kind of obnoxious and bratty. The core of the strategy lies in how you manage your differently-valued people, whether you try to hitch a ride with someone else's boat or commandeer your own destiny, but that wasn't nearly as interesting as I'd hoped it'd be. In any case, I'll try to get it to the table again, but I'm guessing it may not last long in the collection.

Components are pretty and the cardboard is nice and thick (and it's nice that the different terrains have different thickness), but it feels like thick chrome on skimpy game play.

RATING: 10
What a brilliant game!

We played with random initial tile placement, which helps make the game unique every time.

The game is so simple but so perfectly fits the theme of an island self destructing and hoardes of panic stricken tourists rushing to boats and attempting to make their way to safety through whale, sea searpent, and shark infested waters.

What a hoot! Unless someone you play with has had the concept of fun medically removed from their brain, everyone will have one great time with this game.  The component quality is lower than the Escape from Atlantis sequels, but the gameplay is best as written in the original Survive! game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
RECEIVED: 2015

KOREA

Survive is the board game I never knew I wanted when I was a kid. Unfortunately, I didn't find it until 34 years after it first came out. The game play has three basic steps: 

1) Move guys and/or boats
2) Take an available tile and follow the instructions
3) Roll the dice and move a creature

Because it is so simple, it works really well for families. But be careful: unless the people you are playing with have thick skins, you will make enemies. This game is MEAN! And I think that's why gamers might still appreciate this game despite the randomness inherent in the tile-taking or dice-rolling stages of the game.

Along with Takenoko, this is my go-to game for people new to the hobby!

RATING: 7.5
Embrace the mayhem! A favorite of my 7 y.o. Having their explorers eaten may be difficult for some younger players to handle, but usually they seem to enjoy the game enough that playing helps them get over that. Playing with the explorer values hidden is critical so that the game continues to feel competitive to the end. Best at 4p. For 2p games, playing with two colors each is a must to fill the island. Components are very nice. Looks great on the table. Negatives are that the game can drag on a bit if if players don't take their turns quickly, and that the limited movement of the sea creatures can make cautious play an effective if boring option. The latter is fixed by the dive dice expansion. Rating rises to 8 with the expansion.

RATING: 8
In 1982, I really wanted the Milton Bradley electronic board game, Dark Tower, for Christmas.  But with an insane $80 price tag, I did not think anyone would be willing to get it for me.  I asked for this game instead.  At that age, I was intimidated by the complicated-looking rules, so I asked my older brother to explain it to me, and we had a lot of fun with it.

Years later, I made two surprising discoveries:  my brother hadn't explained all the rules correctly, and the game is actually still pretty entertaining.  It's mostly chaos, but there's some mild strategy involved and it's usually pretty tense right up until the end (unless everyone gets their pieces home early).  

The version I own is just titled Survive! and is made by Parker Brothers.  I'd love to get an updated version of it (although the PB version does have really nice components, which have held up very well over the years).

RATING: 6
I have the 30th anniversary edition of this game, and I bought the 6 player expansion at the same time. 
What a great design!
This game works very well at making people mad enough to never want to play it again.
I'm serious.

Don't play it with new gamers. Play this with the same group that plays Cutthroat Caverns - people who don't get their feelings hurt when other players gang up on them. 
This game is the KING of "back-stabbing" game play.
You can't play nice AT ALL. It won't let you.  
Want to see the origins of Forbidden Island?
Here it is.
Want to play a game that ends friendships?  
No you don't.

RATING: 6
Surprisingly good for a Parker Brothers game from the 80s. The rules are simple enough that my four year old can play, but there's enough depth that my gamer friends will play it too.

My daughter and I use the following house rules:

- Skip setup and just put your people wherever.
- The first person to get three people to an island wins.
- Sea creatures are friendly, and they don't like to eat people. (Sometimes I can convince her that they're just taking people off the board for a friendly swim.)

RATING: 8
The venerable Survive has interested me for a long time. When I finally got a chance to play it, it did not disappoint. 

You move your meeples as fast as you can from the sinking island of Atlantis. Pieces are removed from the island each turn, sometimes resulting in your meeples turning into swimmers. Ideally, they will boat to safety, but sometimes swimming is the only option. There's a bit of "take that", but clever play is really more about making friends than making enemies. You want to ride someone else's boat to safety, saving your precious actions for other things. Each piece removed from the island also either causes an event (such as a shark showing up) or goes in your hand and can be played later at an opportune time (such as a dolphin that can push your swimmers quickly to shore). 

The one drawback to the components is the dark-printed number on the bottom of each meeple that is very tough to see, especially on the blue pieces. That said, the very cheap (about $7.50) expansion fixes this and also expands the game to up to six players. That's an incredible bargain. Otherwise, the graphic design, the pieces themselves, and especially the tiles are of excellent quality. Seeing it on the table immediately makes you want to play. Its cute, primary-colored pieces belie the vicious gameplay, yet it is simple enough for almost anyone to get into immediately.

Ultimately, this is one of those games that really can appeal to just about everyone. Kids to adults, gamers to non-gamers, etc. It has that "deep filler" feel that I personally love and I will be adding this to my shelf in the very near future.

RATING: 8
Co-op variant to play with younger kids:

-3 players, or 4 players with only 7 meeples each
-cooperative effort to get as many humans to islands
-ignore the numbers
-at the end of your turn you can give a tile from your hand to another player.
-if a tile has a creature on it, it goes on the spot of the tile
-creatures automatically move to the closest target they can affect
-humans win by outnumbering the creatures in the end

RATING: 9
This game is FUN and very interactive! The fun, and not depth, is the attraction of this game. I have played it with serious games, who enjoyed it, but I believe the typical target group would be families and more casual gamers. 

The game is very confrontational, so it may not be a game for people who dislike direct conflict. You will have to move sharks and sea monsters to eat your opponents' meeples. There is really no down-time, as actions of all other players will change the board and have an impact on your position. Lots of tension and excitement. 

There is some strategy in placing and moving the higher valued meeples, but the luck factor is very high. The good thing is that if you loose, you don't have to feel bad about it - it is not a test of your brain's capacity. 

Prodution quality is top-notch, with a beautiful board, nice wooden components and thick cardboard tiles.

RATING: 7
(05/26/2014) Comment based on 1 play of the reprint.

A well produced, family-accessible, silly-fun game of desperate, panicky, cut-throat goodness that plays within an hour.

You have a bunch of meeples that start off on the sinking island of Atlantis, and you are trying to get them to safety, from the middle to one of the four corners of the board. Each turn, you have three action points to move your meeples onto boats, moving a row boat, or have a meeple swim. another land hex disappears, which can then trigger the spawning of sharks, whales, and vortexes that can eat your swimming meeples, sink your rowboats, or suck up everything within a 1-hex radius. Some tiles can be kept and played later for the players' advantage. However, each turn a special die is thrown, which governs whether a sea serpent (which sinks and eats the meeples), shark, or whale moves, at the player's discretion.

The last part is great fun, as players direct the ever increasing predators at other players' swimming meeples or loaded rowboats carrying survivors. There is a lot of cut-throat action because of this, with lots of yelling and cussing. However, on the bottom of each meeple is a score value (from 1 to 6 VP) that is summed up if the meeple makes it to the safe shores. The other players do not know what which ones are the most valuable, so there is a lot of bluffing and misdirection, in order to get those VIPs out and safe, while sacrificing the lower VP meeples. There is also the "bash the leader", especially if a player has all of their meeples still alive--in this game, no one makes it out with all of their meeples!!!

Simple rules, fast play, little downtime, and great production values make this a pleasure to play. One cannot take this game too seriously, due to the sheer number of predators and high luck factor. You may as well accept it that a lot of your meeples will be eaten, and that there will be a lot of "take that" screwage throughout. If you can get past that, it is quite enjoyable. It is a solid "7".
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Be the drunk guy in the lifeboat with the flare gun and the gas can...  [i]sink it out of spite to kill the other two guys and deny everyone else the boat.[/i]

An ugly little game where the land sloughs off into an ocean boiling with hungry things.  You try to drive your people to safety, everyone else drives the hungry things to their appointed dinners.

Who will make it off the island alive?  The hairdresser or the Nobel Laureate?

My money's on NO ONE.

UPDATE:  The art & design in the new 30th Anniversary Edition are flat-out brilliant.  Also, having uniform plastic meeples is actually better than the misshapen, tippy wooden ones from the previous edition.

RATING: 3
Ideal Players: 2-4

Description: The island is sinking! Get most of your people to shore, avoiding sharks and sea serpents.

Pro: Light and fast game. Fun theme that fits the mechanics perfectly. Neat dynamic of action text under tiles and hidden people values. Each game tells a story, including an imminent sense of peril!

Con: Tiles are a little random. Could use some fresh art and components. No complex strategy involved.

RATING: 9

Yes, you may need the instructions nearby to remind you what exactly your red whale tile does, but I never felt bamboozled by the more experienced player teaching us. Strategy and fortunate timing combined to make a very fun game for us. Bring on more!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
P.B. Edition of Survive(hidden numbers) 

What a neat little awesome themed game that I really wish I could have played in 1982 instead of discovering in 2007, THE THEME IS THE GAME, no paste-up here.

Everyone starts on an island (made up of tiles) and the object is to get to shore as fast as possible by swimming or boat. The need to go fast is due to all the lurking dangers, Whales, Sharks and Sea serpents in the water.  The island starts sinking one tile at a time until a Volcano tile is turned over and then the game ends as the Volcano destroys everything left on the board. Who ever has the highest total on their survivors wins.

Simple rules and very fast turns make up this game.  Really almost ahead of its time and quite compariable to games nowadays with 3 action points per turn, hidden values of your men which can induce a bluffing effect, a great dose of screwage and a modular board. The game has a big dose of luck and some randomness which should but lethal together but it really doesn't detract here, it is a 45 minute to one hour light and fun game that would make a great gateway game (leave out over sensitive people maybe though).  

The memory element is optional; my memory sucks so I like playing without it. I also think playing without the hidden values wouldn't  be as fun, easy to fix if you get the other version.  Oh, it is not all luck either, there are some important timing aspects, small decisions and anticipation of where your opponents are hiding their big value people.  Some nice tension created with the monsters in the sea, uncertainty in the tile flip and the unknown time factor near the end. 

Best with four I think, then 3 but playable 2 - 4 (2 with 2 colours each best). A little more control with 2 and more chaotic with 4 but then that is part of the fun here. Not to be overlooked due to age and well worth seeking out if a light fast fun game with screwage sounds good to you. Very comparable to Pompei which I intend to play very soon, will update after playing it.

RATING: 4
1982!  Take another look at this one:  it is really a German-style game in Parker Brothers clothing.  Perhaps that's why it flopped in the U.S. marketplace way back when.  I'm glad my wife held onto her childhood copy of it.  Not quite as interesting as a more modern game, but certainly amazing from a historical perspective.  If you look at the board without your glasses on, you might see a shadow of Settlers lurking there (a hex-tile island with several terrain types---of course, in SURVIVE!, you're trying to escape from the island, not colonize it.  SURVIVE! is a bit like Settlers run backward).

RATING: 6
2012-04-27

Initial Rating: 8.0 (May 2011)

Good game that can lead to hurt feelings, I like it a lot because I love confrontational games. The Stronghold edition is very well done EXCEPT for the quality of the  figures. I have played with 3 different copies and they all had some broken component (Stronghold always replaced the damaged components). The game offers lots of fun in a reasonable time frame. I´m not sure about adding more players with the expansion though.

Survive is not a deep game, it´s main appeal is the “take that” factor but I also like the temporal alliances and negotiation needed to win.

If I play I want to play with the hidden values under my meeples, that makes the game a lot more strategic for me.

Current Rating: 8.0
[hr]
2013-03-07

I downgraded the rating to a 7.0 because this is not a game I want to play all the time, only occasionally. Still Survive is a good game.

This way it reflects better my feelings toward the game and it matches the BGG ranking system.

Current Rating: 7.0 
[hr]
2013-05-03

Nowadays, I almost never want to play survive, It is a good game but I don’t want to play it, so for now I’m downgrading its rating to a 6.0. I sold my new copy. I want to play this around once every 6 months. 

Current Rating: 6.0

RATING: 5
2013-03-07

Initial Rating: 7.0

This comment is for the 30 Anniversary edition. 

I’m a little disappointed that Stronghold  decided to take some things from the game (the Dive Dice, and the Dolphins), the core stuff is still there, but knowing that this edition has less variants than the previous one, (somehow) detracts from the game for me. To be congruent with my ratings, I’m downgrading this to a 6.5.

The only positive are the plastic meeples with CLEARLY read numbers on their bases.

I’m neutral on the art change.

If I’m buying Survive, I will buy the 2011 edition. 

Current Rating: 6.5

2013-05-03

To be congruent with my ratings, I’m downgrading the rating of this edition as well. Stronghold is selling the missing components as promo expansions, I don’t agree much with this policy as the old game had them in it. This rating reflects the fact that I want to play the game perhaps every 6 months AND that I consider this new edition to be inferior to the previous one.

RATING: 8
There are three sets of players for this game - 1)  AP-Prone Eurogamers - they will hate it, 2) Kids (the intended audience) - they will love it, and 3) Hardcore AT gamers.....they will love it, hate it, and then realize what is, and then love it again.  This is a knife-fight in a phone booth.  Nothing special and winning/losing isn't the point - it's all about screwage of your friends and neighbors.  I love it, my kid loves it, what else matters?  I wouldn't play it for money but that's not the point, is it?

RATING: 8
There is a movie called "There will be blood".  In this game, there will be blood.  You'll be sending sharks to eat your competition, sending sea monsters to take out boats full of people who were just about to reach safety, and generally doing anything annoying to undermine your opponents.  

Table flipping may occur.

Just recently I had two of my most valuable survivors in a boat just two actions away from being safe and ensuring my win.  A sea monster sat right next to the boat.  It was a risk i was willing to take.  I survived everyone's turn except the very last die roll of the person to my right.  She sent the sea monster to dine on my points and she won the game instead.  AHHHHHHH!!!

RATING: 7
WAF : 10
4p (3-4)
60M
1.71/5

+ Easy rules
+ Fast gameplay

- Huge luck factor (turn tile get shark, roll dice, move shark)
- All vs One can have (combined with a bit of luck) huge impact when it happens wich ruins your game.
- Component quality (asmodee)

We found the dive dice from the expansion to be clunky.
As dived creatures must spawn at empty space it is only good for the squid or moving other monsters away. Can be meh when rolling to many dive dice.

:star::star::star::star::star::star::star::halfstar::nostar::nostar: 7.5/10 IF with 4 players AND good group.

RATING: 6
[size=12][b]Top 200 board games list[/b][/size]

[size=12][b]Why I like Survive: Escape from Atlantis![/b][/size]
+ I like how the "take that" is often spread out among all of the players so nobody feels targeted. 
+ I like the randomness in this game (a rarity) because the game is supposed to be a lightweight family game whereby the most strategic player can lose. 
+ I like the theme
+ The game is short
+ The game is easy to teach
+ The game has decent replayability.

[size=12][b]Fixable dislikes in regards to Survive: Escape from Atlantis![/b][/size]
/ I dislike memory games. There are nonetheless a few cheats you can use like rotating the meeples or positioning the higher values in a distinct spot
/ The rulebook is lacking. The FAQ I made addresses this issue. 
/ I would like the game more if the game had some extra land tiles so that certain tiles are randomly out of the game. I am a fan of variable set-ups after all. I suppose that I could get a second copy of the base game. 

[size=12][b]Why I dislike Survive: Escape from Atlantis![/b][/size]
- I would like the game more if there were variant green dolphin tiles (so that you can still use the red dolphin tiles) and if the whale tile referred to the squid too. I cannot fix this issue. 

[size=12][b]VERDICT:[/b] Keep & Sometimes willing to play this game[/size]

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Survive is a cutthroat game where players seek to evacuate their pieces from an island that is breaking up, while remembering where their highest-valued pieces are located to maximize their score.

An island made up of 40 hex-tiles is slowly sinking into the ocean (as the tiles are removed from the board). Each player controls ten people (valued from 1 to 6) that they try and move towards the safety of the surrounding islands before the main island finally blows up. Players can either swim or use boats to travel but must avoid sea serpents, whales and sharks on their way to safety.

RATING: N/A

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
* Components
+ Nice, very thick tiles
- The meeples do not have the same shape, so it is not hard to remember which one is the 6-valued one, for instance.  Given the fact that meeple values must be remembered, players are actually encouraged to distinguish physical differences between meeples, and can learn them.  Giving players the same color each time helps, as they do not learn the value of the other player's meeples.
- One sea serpent was broken.  I glued the pieces.
- Two tiles had a creased corner, which makes the recognizable, which is not great.
- The box cover was new but damage: the paper covering was broken on the edge, because it creases (?) instead of bending.

* Feelings
- The luck factor is quite high, but there is room for more clever move and for some strategy. Some optimal moves are sometimes not seen immediately: the game requires some concentration, and sometimes some (limited) creativity.
+ The game is very thematic, which helps remembering the rules. Even somewhat counter-intuitive rules ("Squids like dry food only").
- The rulebook is quite complete (the FAQ is not too long), but the information is presented in an "item by item" fashion that does not give the big picture (for instance, I had missed the fact that Dolphins move along with Swimmers, because it was drowned in a list of a dozen points instead of being logically place closed to the "The Dolphins are the good guys" point.
+ The atmosphere of the game is light, with a lot of schadenfreude, exclamations, etc. A nice family game.
+ Setup and game play are both quite fast.

RATING: 7
Great light family game. With the 5-6 player expansion this game becomes extremely versatile. It plays best 3-5 players though. Success in the game is determined in part by luck (roll of the monster dice, good tile draws) but winning the game is often secondary to laughing with each other about your misfortunes. The game becomes a riot when people start naming their people and providing back stories before they meet a tragic fate with the sharks.

RATING: 8

I still have this, but all the stickers fell off the meeples so it is no longer playable.


BETRAYAL. Simple, fun rules and a strong theme with lots of laughs.  Players control an army of little meeples that try to get off the island but also make decisions for monsters that move every turn, so players get pitted against each other while trying to save themselves.  A hex from the island is removed every turn, adding to the fun. This is a great game for casual players or a dinner party.

I really like this game, so I'm reluctant to trade it.  However, I know there's a lot of people who want this original edition, which includes the dolphin and dive dice.  I don't use them when I play, so I might be willing to trade this and buy myself a copy of the new set later on. 

This also includes the 5-6 player expansion pack.

RATING: 6
One of the most vicious and cutthroat games I have ever played.  Lots of way to screw over your friends, but surprisingly very diplomatic.  Table talk is highly encouraged and you will need to temporarily ally with people, otherwise you will have the entire board against you.  Extremely easy to teach and does fall within the 30 to 45 minute timeframe.  The only main issue with the game is it doesn't have a lot of meat to it, so gamers who want a more thinking involved in a 45 minute timeframe could look at other options like King of New York or Ra.

RATING: 9
Survive is exactly what it sounds like: pure, lighthearted fun, with lots of opportunities for screwing each other over, narrow escapes, and surprises.

Bluffing about the value of your people (as well as potentially forgetting their value) and holding tiles for later use add some strategy, and the game is short enough and simple enough that it feels just right.

The 3D effect created by the varying tile heights is nice, and the components are top-notch across the board.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
LOVE this game! What a classic! If you're into blood sport, Survive is right up your alley. This game is straight-up brutal, but so much fun. You have to go into it with a light heart. Otherwise, the game could escalate into a brawl/divorce, depending on who you are playing with. Typically, I'm not a big fan of direct conflict in games. I only like direct conflict in light games or games that are specifically designed to create conflict. This games meet both criteria. It's fun and light, but it's also supposed to be confrontational. Survive also affords a surprising amount of strategic planning. To be sure, a good memory assists in this planning, but it's not necessary to play well. Add great bits, smooth gameplay and play time under 1 hour, and this gem jumps from great to fantastic. 

P.S. I've only played this as a 2 player so far. I can't wait to play with more!

Update 4/26/14: 

I played with 4 tonight. To be honest, I don't know that it's better with 4 than 2. There's definitely more chaos and less strategy (due to lack of control). It just depends on what type of mood you are in. If you want a straight-up brawl, then 4 is very good. But if you're in the mood for a cutthroat, albeit fun chess match, then two is perfect.

RATING: 8
Good family fun.  My 8 year old relishes the potential for screwage, whilst the entire thing is simple enough for my 6 year old to cope with as well.  Very very popular.  And the in box dolphin expansion makes it even better.

Disappointments mainly from  slightly off production quality:  Meeples roughly hewn and poorly painted; board hefty but easily dinged and scuffed (a problem for a sliding round the board meeple based game -a harder linen finish would have been much more sensible;mountain pieces poorly printed/cut (the latter sorted by the 5/6 expansion - a bonus undermined by the meeple in that expansion being plastic with paper base stickers.

Almost perfect; but would have benefited from as much care in the manufacture as in the (re)design.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Fantastic game. Forget strategy and swim for it! Seriously, a fun, laugh out loud game as you cheer your meeples on, hoping they won’t get eaten. 

Definitely best with 3 or 4 people so you get more interaction (and more bad things!) but does play fine with 2 as well. 

This is all about theme as you imagine Jaws or the Loch Ness Monster coming after everyone. If you’re actually thinking about which meeples have the high point values, you’re doing it wrong – focus on the fun people!

Though the random tiles and dice make each game different, it’s really the same. As such, there can be too much of a good thing, but it’s fun to bring out from time to time to goof off. 

Great production value – nice board, components and rule book.  Easy to teach/learn, plays quick. No bash the leader and no AP issues.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
A little gem of a game. A remake of the 1980 classic Parker Bros game. It's not complicated and it's somewhat random but it's extremely playable. 

Stronghold has re-issued it with really beautiful components. You race to get your wooden meeples off the sinking island of Atlantis and see them swim or boat to safety on neighbouring atolls.

Each island tile you sink has a hazard on the other side, in the form of whales, sharks, whirlpools and sea serpents which go into the water and come after your swimmers. You win this game by eating your opponent's meeples before they can get to safety. Fun! Ok with two.  Best with four.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6.5
A bit confrontational which is typically not my thing, but the game is light and fun enough that it doesn't bother me here.  I also like the memorization aspect of placing the meeples, although I'm terrible at remembering most of mine.  The varied-depth hex tiles are fantastic and the overall play feels tight and engaging.  The meeple components could be better -- the originals varied in size a bit, potentially "marking" them.  The replacements with the 5-6 player add-on were consistently-sized but had little paint smudges on them, presenting them same problem.  Overall, great game if you want something lightweight with a nice mix of temporary alliances, occasional back-stabbing, and some luck.

RATING: 6.5
There is certainly a kind of maniacal glee that goes along with this game, something I haven't seen in other games of this type, cutthroat games.  Usually leading to hurt feelings in my group (and hence a leaning toward more cooperative or one v many games), this one has taken root in our group as a new fan-favorite.  Watching the dice get rolled every turn and hoping "notmenotmenotmenotme" never seems to get old, and has the added effect of somehow causing folks not to hate the guy who just capsized their boat with the whale, but immediately regroup and come up with a new strategy.  For its age (I have the old 1982 PB copy), it is WAY ahead of its time and has held up exceedingly well.  Survive is a pretty grim world if you think about it, but it is incredibly fun and uncomplicated.

RATING: 6
Game in a Nutshell: Escape from a dissolving island by securing spots on boats and evading a number of monsters in your way.

Played as: 4 player.

Pros: The theme fits this game like a glove. The race for the boats instills a sense of panic as if the island really was disintegrating under your own feet. Conflict and tension is forced upon players; sometimes so much that it feels better to see the other boats fall victim to a sea monster then relief of getting your own men home safe.

Cons: Awful rule book, don't count on knowing what should happen towards the end of the game. Possibly could benefit from some streamlining: less pawns to move and a smaller island could cause things to pick up as there would be fewer choices to make with the limited actions given. As is, the whole game could come to a screeching halt with only one AP player.

Other: I wish I would have known they made games like this back in the day. I think even a modern remake would stand for some positive attention today.

Best Use: I'm guessing there would be no finer use for this then as a family game with the kids.

RATING: 8
The 8 rating is based on several plays, mostly with two players. It is light, fun, easy to learn and entertained the whole family. A neat game idea, well executed.

If all Euros aspired to this level of quality, tension, screwage and theme, the genre wouldn't be so laughably lame to me. It proves that Euro and Euroish games can have interesting themes with well-matched mechanics that--gasp!--make it fun to play. There are no viziers or brown cubes or granaries or textile markets to be seen here. Just frickin' sharks and sea monsters gobbling up swimmers as an island sinks into the ocean. 

The new edition looks great and (I think, maybe I'm wrong) has a few unnecessary changes and additions. There was nothing wrong or in need of fixing about the old edition. Not that the new edition is bad, but...why?

RATING: 6
26-Jan-2014:  I still this is a great game and would recommend it to any family or group looking for a light-hearted, fun gotcha-style of game.

Unfortunately, my family doesn't seem to enjoy the "gotcha" aspect of this game, even though it's all in good fun.  Because of this, we've only played this game twice in 2013 and not since June.  My kids, and even my wife, get annoyed when I send Sharks and Whales after their little Meeples.  And if I take out a boat that has both my dude and someone else's because I know it's a high scoring one...yikes!  I'm in trouble then.

I try to explain to them, that's the whole point of the game.  Meeples get eaten throughout the game!  It's all just for fun.

Oh well.  Just keep that in mind.  If your group can't handle direct conflict, even with cute little Shark meeples and Sea Monsters, then I'm sad to say this may not work for you.

If that's not an issue, then this game is great, and has awesome components.  Go get it.

08-Feb-2013: This was a family favorite...at first.  This was another one of my early purchases when getting into the hobby and my family definitely enjoyed it.  The gameplay was unique to use with the sinking island.  The components are fabulous with the various sharks, whales, sea monsters, meeples, and boats all made of wood.

Everyone starts with 10 people on a sinking island and you must get as many as you can to surrounding land before the volcano on the island explodes.  Each meeple has a point value assigned to it, and you'll have to remember who is who throughout the game as the numbers are hidden during play.  Unfortunately, all of the players are allowed to control the various sea creatures in the water which attack your meeples, eating them up and destroying the boats they are using to escape.

If you do not like direct conflict, you may not like this game.  As I said, my family really liked this at first.  It was so different and new to us, no one payed attention to the direct attacks between players.  But over time and several plays, my wife and kids became less enamored when their meeples would be devoured by a sea monster.  I always played the game as a light, fun experience where you expect to lose a lot of your pawns.  If you take it as a fun, family gotcha game, you should get a lot out of this.  If you take it too seriously, you could be in trouble with your kids.

RATING: 8
MAYHEM! Must DIY this. Look, this is clearly not a modern design - for one thing, the variation in point values of the little guys is a bit much, and it was suggested that there would be more strategy if one could peek at those values during the game. But, it's really just about perfect for what it is. You're going to lose a lot of guys. So you have to make tough choices. There's lots of screwage, and it's done right. And, as my daughter observed, the different point values do essentially remove any potential kingmaker problem. Plus cool bits... it's just sweet.

+.5 the boats combined with indiscriminate threats add a small element of collaboration and collusion 

+.5 novelty of eating drowning seamen with sharks or sea-monsters and general 'gotcha!' mechanics are done in a  satisfying and fun way

-2 beyond the subtle stuff, it's not too deep strategy wise, and isn't the most repayable game ever. 
 

A fun game to break out in groups that like novel themes and shallow (no pun intended) dudes on a map games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This Euro-thematic hybrid is very popular. Making use of a modular board, Escape requires the players to get a team of their people off the island, which slowly sinks over time, to the safety of the 4 distant forms of land in the corner of the board. 

What makes the game so much fun is that the players have duel roles. As well as trying to save as many of their people as possible, they are also trying to help kill the meeple of their opponents. 

They can do this by moving the various sharks, whales and squids to intercept meeple. 

The other thing going for the game is that each meeple a person controls is worth a certain value. Those points are only earned when a meeple gets to safety. So the players are trying to kill as many enemy meeple as possible, but they really want to stop the high-valued ones from getting to safety. 

This can lead to all manner of mind games as the players try to bluff and double bluff by making moves that may seem like a meeple is worth high points when in fact it isn't. 

This is good family fun and kids particularly delight in wiping out their parents meeple.

RATING: 9.3
I don't know exactly what it is about this game, but it makes it to the table more often than most of my collection. Some of the things I like about it:
Visually gorgeous
Great Bits
Relaxed quick gameplay (usally 2 players controlling 2 colors each)
The "take that" aspect doesn't feel personal or vindictive...if your swimming in shark infested waters, you should expect the inevitable. ;)
There is just enough strategy and sneakyness to make it feel strategy rather than luck driven.
The theme and mechanics mesh perfectly.

All said, this is one of my favorite light weight games. :)

RATING: 5
Survive: Escape From Atlantis is easy to learn, simple to play, has beautiful components, and I don't want to own it. The game-play is well structured and achieves exactly the experience it sets out to. Unfortunately it is not an experience that I enjoy.

S:EfA is just too mean. To win you must kill off other players meeples and, as the meeples value is hidden, you need to kill off several to feel confident of any kind of lead. This kind of assurance is rarely felt, so players will literally wipe out boatloads of competitors meeples even to the point of wiping out all of a player's meeples.

Games that induce a 'To win I must kill you' feeling I don't enjoy.

RATING: 8
[b]Survive[/b] was traded away in a math trade 3/17/15. (Received Camel Up) Back in the collection and was sold via auction 10/15/16.

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]Unfortunately this stopped seeing play in favor of other gateway games with extended family (Camel Up and Diamant to name a few) so I traded it away. In my opinion this is still a great game to introduce to family and friends that are new to the hobby. I definitely prefer it over The Downfall of Pompeii. My kids inquired about this game recently and said they missed playing it. Fortunately I was able to pick up a copy in a local math trade.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- A great introductory family game as long as your family can deal with some take that game play.
- I have found that it plays well with 2, we each play 3 colors and use the overcrowded variant. This helps ensure lots of meeples getting eaten.
- Extremely easy to teach, making it a great family game.
- Beautiful components, especially the sea creatures.[/i]

With 2 players we play with the variant of drawing 2 tiles per turn. It is perfect and doesn't in any way disturb the game.

RATING: 3
What I liked:
- Great components

What I didn't like:
- Cutthroat play. People have said it doesn't feel cutthroat, but they are wrong.
- Highly random, which is ok in a filler, but not in a 90 minute game like the one we had.
- Too long. A 4p learning game of a random filler like this should be 45 minutes tops.
- Too confusing to be a great gateway game.
- The pacing is not great, as you can have all the boats show up at the end, or on one side of the board.

I would put the weight a bit higher than 1.7, as it is definitely harder to understand than Forbidden Island or Jaipur.

RATING: 7
*** Traded for Arkadia ***

$35

--- Includes 5&6player expansion ---

Initial 2 player game with girlfriend made me feel this game deserves a 7/10 rating. Maybe it needs a little bit more players to make it chaotic and fun. 

It is a very nice game with a bit of "take that". The confrontation feels pretty not personal since the game requires us to play it in a very cut throat-y manner. I think this game is a good training wheel game to get my family members to get used to "take that" mechanics in games. They need to learn it is nothing personal.

---- Update ----
Played a 6 player game, the game drags a bit long, but is more fun in the "meta-game" side where negotiation and back-stabbing happens compared to a 2-player game.
Rating goes up from 7 to 8.

---- Update ----
With lukewarm reaction from the game group after only handful of plays this drops back down to a 7. I think this is not suitable for our game group because couples don't turn on each other and in result makes the game bland and unbalanced.

---- Update ----
This is definitely a "depends on your game group" kind of game. My family is not that kind of in your face group so this couldn't hit the table and 2-player with fiancee is just straight mean. Traded in a math trade.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a very cute game, where players get meeples with different scoring numbers printed at the base. On a player's turn they remove part of the island, then move some of their meeples, trying to escape to the safe shores, then the roll a die to determine what monsters they activate if any. The quality of the components in the edition I had was quite nice, but no matter how many times I play this game, I can never remember which of my meeples are high scoring and which are low. The game plays like a chaotic mess. Players are incentivized to work together to escape on the boats, but only one player ultimately wins. The monster effects wind up being a blind punch the player you feel like punching, since your opponents have no idea about what your score is until the end of the game.

This is a funny game that doesn't last too long, but after 7 plays I got tired of it. It's not normally my sort of game, but it was worth a laugh for awhile.

:star: Art and components
:star: Innovative mechanics
:star: Handles 5 or more players
:star: Good with min or max players
:star: Low time between turns
:star: Comfortable complexity
:star: Re-playability
:star::nostar::nostar: Enjoyment

RATING: 7.9
This game was a great additon to my teenage games playing--our family loved it! A charming premise of getting your people off a sinking island (swimming or in boats), avoiding pitfalls like sharks, whales, sea-monsters, whirlpools and finally, the volcanic explosion! Nice game play wraps in around an hour. Much more fun with 4 people as the island sinks more quickly. (Each turn someone removes one hexagonal island piece, starting with beaches, then forest, then mountain. The more people playing the faster the island sinks.)

RATING: 10
Cutthroat but cute.

It's so cute that nobody minds dying a sudden death, especially if there's some story and monster noise for entertainment too. lol.

When the boat is filled with three meeples each from different players, we call that the "international" boat. Usually, the international boat goes nowhere. lol. Also, when a boat has two of the player's colors, we call that "juicy". They are usually eaten because it's so tempting. Best survival chance is alone or with another player.

RATING: 8
I remember my best mate getting the original version of this game for Christmas back when it came out in 1986. I LOVED the game back then. As the years went by, I quite forgot about the fun we had playing this one - so imagine my suprise when I went to a games convention and found this game in the games library that we could play! Well, I couldn't grab the game quickly enough :) 

For me, this review is a mix of objectiveness and nostalgia. The current incarnation hasn't changed that much from the original version I remember (the spinner for moving creatures is now a dice, the middle island could be a lot more random back then). The game is fairly simple to play, basically just moving your people as quickly as you can to the safety of the islands on the edges of the board. But the ability to send monsters to interfere with your opponents is where the fun of this game comes in! Of course, it's not so much fun when they send a shark towards your clump of swimmers.....

Overall, I think this is a great game to play once in a while. While not a go-to game, it is a great "lighter" game - one to play between heavier thinking games perhaps. Probably deserves a 7, but it gets an extra point from me for the extreme nostalgia factor!
